SENATE BILL No. 27
A BILL FOR AN ACT to amend the Indiana Code concerning state
and local administration and to make an appropriation.
Be it enacted by the General Assembly of the State of Indiana:
1 SECTION 1. IC 5-1-17.1 IS ADDED TO THE INDIANA CODE
2 AS A NEW CHAPTER TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
3 UPON PASSAGE]:
4 Chapter 17.1. Northwest Indiana Stadium Authority
5 Sec. 0.3. The general assembly finds the following:
6 (1) Northwest Indiana as a region and the city face unique and
7 distinct challenges and opportunities related to the economic
8 development issues associated with the construction and
9 maintenance of a world-class stadium facility in the city.
10 (2) A unique approach is required to ensure that northwest
11 Indiana has sufficient revenue sources to allow it to meet these
12 challenges and opportunities.
13 (3) The powers and responsibilities provided to northwest
14 Indiana and to the northwest Indiana stadium authority
15 created by this chapter are appropriate and necessary to
16 carry out the public purposes of encouraging and fostering
17 economic development in northwest Indiana and constructing
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

2
1 a world-class stadium facility in the city.
2 (4) The relocation of a National Football League franchised
3 professional football team in northwest Indiana poses unique
4 challenges due to the need for development of a world-class
5 football stadium and related infrastructure that would not be
6 needed apart from the needs related to the relocation of a
7 National Football League franchised professional football
8 team in the city.
9 (5) The relocation of a National Football League franchised
10 professional football team in the city is critical to successful
11 economic development in the city and northwest Indiana and
12 is a public purpose.
13 (6) Encouragement of economic development in northwest
14 Indiana will:
15 (A) provide significant economic activity, a substantial
16 portion of which results from persons residing outside
17 Indiana, which may attract new businesses and encourage
18 existing businesses to remain or expand in the city and
19 northwest Indiana;
20 (B) promote the city and northwest Indiana to residents
21 outside Indiana, which may attract residents outside
22 Indiana and new businesses to relocate to the city and
23 northwest Indiana area;
24 (C) protect and increase state and local tax revenues; and
25 (D) encourage overall economic growth in northwest
26 Indiana and in Indiana.
27 (7) Northwest Indiana faces unique challenges in the
28 development of infrastructure and other facilities necessary
29 to promote economic development:
30 (A) as a result of its need to rely on sources of revenue
31 other than property taxes;
32 (B) due to the large number of tax exempt properties
33 located in northwest Indiana; and
34 (C) because northwest Indiana is the site of numerous state
35 and regional nonprofit corporations.
36 (8) Economic development benefits the health and welfare of
37 the people of Indiana, is a public use and purpose for which
38 public money may be spent, and is of public utility and
39 benefit.
40 Sec. 1. As used in this chapter, "authority" refers to the
41 northwest Indiana stadium authority created by this chapter.
42 Sec. 2. As used in this chapter, "board" refers to the board of
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

3
1 directors of the authority.
2 Sec. 3. As used in this chapter, "bonds" means bonds, notes,
3 commercial paper, or other evidences of indebtedness. The term
4 includes obligations (as defined in IC 8-9.5-9-3) and swap
5 agreements (as defined in IC 8-9.5-9-4).
6 Sec. 4. As used in this chapter, "capital improvement" means
7 the building, facilities, or improvements that the board determines
8 will be of general public benefit or welfare and will promote the
9 cultural, recreational, public, or civic well-being of the city and
10 northwest Indiana. This includes the land comprising the site,
11 equipment, heating and air conditioning facilities, sewage disposal
12 facilities, landscaping, walks, drives, parking facilities, and other
13 structures, facilities, appurtenances, materials, and supplies that
14 are necessary to make any building, facility, or improvement
15 suitable for the use for which it was constructed.
16 Sec. 4.2. As used in this chapter, "city" means the city of
17 Hammond, Indiana.
18 Sec. 4.5. As used in this chapter, "stadium board" refers to the
19 northwest Indiana stadium board created by 36-10-9.5.
20 Sec. 5. As used in this chapter, "state agency" means any of the
21 following:
22 (1) An authority, a board, a commission, a committee, a
23 department, a division, or other instrumentality of state
24 government.
25 (2) The Indiana finance authority created by IC 5-1.2-3.
26 Sec. 6. A northwest Indiana stadium authority is hereby created
27 as a separate body corporate and politic as an instrumentality of
28 the state to acquire, construct, equip, own, lease, and finance
29 facilities for lease to or for the benefit of the stadium board. The
30 Indiana finance authority shall provide staff support to the board
31 of directors appointed under section 7 of this chapter.
32 Sec. 7. (a) The board is composed of the following members who
33 must be residents of Indiana:
34 (1) The director of the state budget agency, or the director's
35 designee, who shall serve as chair of the board.
36 (2) One (1) member appointed by the executive of the city,
37 who shall serve as the vice chair of the board.
38 (3) The public finance director or the director's designee.
39 (b) If Lake County adopts an ordinance imposing a food and
40 beverage tax pursuant to IC 6-9-36-3 and adopts an ordinance
41 increasing the Lake County innkeeper's tax pursuant to
42 IC 6-9-2-1.5, the following two (2) members shall be added to the

4
1 board:
2 (1) One (1) member appointed by the county executive of
3 Lake County.
4 (2) One (1) member selected by the public finance director

6 (c) If Porter County adopts an ordinance imposing a food and
7 beverage tax pursuant to IC 6-9-36-3, the following two (2)
8 members shall be added to the board:
9 (1) One (1) member appointed by the county executive of
10 Porter County.
11 (2) One (1) member selected by the public finance director

1 (1) continues to serve after the expiration of the appointment

11 Sec. 8. (a) The board shall hold an annual organizational
12 meeting.
13 (b) The board shall elect one (1) member secretary-treasurer to
14 perform the duties of those offices. The secretary-treasurer shall
15 serve from the date of the member's election and until the
16 member's successor is elected and qualified.
17 (c) Special meetings may be called by the chair of the board.
18 (d) The following apply:
19 (1) Two (2) members constitute a quorum, if no members are
20 appointed to the board under section 7(b) and 7(c) of this
21 chapter.
22 (2) Three (3) members constitute a quorum, if members are
23 appointed to the board under one (1) but not both section 7(b)
24 and 7(c) of this chapter.
25 (3) Four (4) members constitute a quorum, if members are
26 appointed to the board under both section 7(b) and 7(c) of this
27 chapter.
28 The concurrence of a majority of the members is necessary to
29 authorize any action.
30 (e) Subject to IC 5-14-1.5-3.6, members of the board may
31 participate in a meeting of the board by electronic communication.
32 Sec. 9. (a) The board may adopt the bylaws and rules it
33 considers necessary for the proper conduct of its duties and the
34 safeguarding of the funds and property entrusted to its care.
35 (b) The board shall, without complying with IC 4-22-2, adopt
36 the code of ethics in executive order 05-12 for its members and
37 employees.
38 Sec. 9.5. The members, officers and employees of the authority
39 executing bonds, leases, obligations, or other agreements under this
40 chapter are not subject to personal liability or accountability by
41 reason of any act authorized by this chapter.
42 Sec. 10. The authority is organized for the following purposes:

6
1 (1) Acquiring, financing, constructing, and leasing land and
2 capital improvements to or for the benefit of the stadium
3 board.
4 (2) Financing and constructing additional improvements to
5 capital improvements owned by the authority and leasing
6 them to or for the benefit of the stadium board.
7 (3) Acquiring land or all or a portion of one (1) or more
8 capital improvements from the stadium board by purchase or
9 lease and leasing the land or these capital improvements back
10 to the stadium board, with any additional improvements that
11 may be made to them.
12 (4) Acquiring all or a portion of one (1) or more capital
13 improvements from the stadium board by purchase or lease
14 to fund or refund indebtedness incurred on account of those
15 capital improvements to enable the stadium board to make a
16 savings in debt service obligations or lease rental obligations
17 or to obtain relief from covenants that the stadium board
18 considers to be unduly burdensome.
19 Sec. 11. (a) The authority may also:

23 (2) lease the land or those capital improvements to the

20 The resolution is conclusive evidence of the public necessity of the
21 proposed acquisition and shall be referred to the attorney general
22 for action, in the name of the authority, in the circuit or superior

24 Sec. 12. (a) Bonds issued under IC 36-10-9.5 or prior law may

33 (2) sell all or a portion of land or a capital improvement or

36 capital improvement or improvements from the authority.

14 Sec. 17. (a) The stadium board may lease for a nominal lease

21 board.
22 (c) The stadium board may sell property to the authority.
23 Sec. 18. (a) Subject to subsection (h), the authority may issue
24 bonds for the purpose of obtaining money to pay the cost of:
25 (1) acquiring real or personal property, including existing
26 capital improvements;
27 (2) constructing, improving, reconstructing, or renovating one
28 (1) or more capital improvements; or
29 (3) funding or refunding bonds issued under IC 36-10-9.5 or
30 prior law.
31 (b) The bonds are payable from the lease rentals from the lease
32 of the capital improvements for which the bonds were issued,
33 insurance proceeds, and any other funds pledged or available.
34 (c) The bonds shall be authorized by a resolution of the board.
35 (d) The terms and form of the bonds shall either be set out in the
36 resolution or in a form of trust indenture approved by the
37 resolution.
38 (e) The bonds shall mature within forty (40) years.
39 (f) The board shall sell the bonds at public or private sale upon
40 the terms determined by the board.
41 (g) All money received from any bonds issued under this
42 chapter shall be applied to the payment of the cost of the

1 (or its successor agency) and the public finance director

1 (A) A log of the dates and times of each meeting with the
2 bidder.

9 secrets, manufacturing processes, and financial information
10 that was not required to be made available for public
11 inspection by the terms of the invitation for bids.
12 Sec. 19. This chapter contains full and complete authority for
13 the issuance of bonds. No law, procedure, proceedings,
14 publications, notices, consents, approvals, orders, or acts by the
15 board or any other officer, department, agency, or instrumentality
16 of the state or of any political subdivision is required to issue any
17 bonds, except as prescribed in this chapter.
18 Sec. 20. Bonds issued under this chapter are legal investments
19 for private trust funds and the funds of banks, trust companies,
20 insurance companies, building and loan associations, credit unions,
21 banks of discount and deposit, savings banks, loan and trust and
22 safe deposit companies, rural loan and savings associations,
23 guaranty loan and savings associations, mortgage guaranty
24 companies, small loan companies, industrial loan and investment
25 companies, and other financial institutions organized under
26 Indiana law.
27 Sec. 21. (a) The authority may secure bonds issued under this
28 chapter by a trust indenture between the authority and a corporate
29 trustee, which may be any trust company or national or bank
30 having the powers of a trust company in Indiana.
31 (b) The trust indenture may:
32 (1) pledge or assign lease rentals, receipts, and income from
33 leased capital improvements, but may not mortgage land or
34 capital improvements;
35 (2) contain reasonable and proper provisions for protecting
36 and enforcing the rights and remedies of the bondholders,
37 including covenants setting forth the duties of the authority
38 and board;
39 (3) set forth the rights and remedies of bondholders and
40 trustee; and
41 (4) restrict the individual right of action of bondholders.
42 (c) Any pledge or assignment made by the authority under this
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

14
1 section is valid and binding from the time that the pledge or
2 assignment is made, against all persons whether or not they have
3 notice of the lien. Any trust indenture by which a pledge is created
4 or an assignment made need not be filed or recorded. The lien is
5 perfected against third parties by filing the trust indenture in the
6 records of the board.
7 Sec. 22. If the stadium board exercises its option to purchase
8 leased property, it may issue its bonds as authorized by statute.
9 Sec. 23. All:
10 (1) property owned by the authority;
11 (2) property leased to or by the authority;
12 (3) revenues of the authority; and
13 (4) bonds issued by the authority, the interest on the bonds,
14 the proceeds received by a holder from the sale of bonds to
15 the extent of the holder's cost of acquisition, proceeds received
16 upon redemption before maturity, proceeds received at
17 maturity, and the receipt of interest in proceeds;
18 are exempt from taxation in Indiana for all purposes except the
19 financial institutions tax imposed under IC 6-5.5.
20 Sec. 24. Any action to contest the validity of bonds to be issued
21 under this chapter may not be brought after the fifteenth day
22 following:
23 (1) the receipt of bids for the bonds, if the bonds are sold at
24 public sale; or
25 (2) the publication one (1) time in a newspaper of general
26 circulation published in either Lake County or Porter County
27 of notice of the execution and delivery of the contract for the
28 sale of bonds;
29 whichever occurs first.
30 Sec. 24.1. The authority shall not issue bonds to finance any
31 capital improvement in the city unless the fiscal body of the city
32 imposes the tax authorized by IC 6-9-78-2 by the maximum
33 amount authorized by IC 6-9-78-3(a).
34 Sec. 25. (a) Notwithstanding any other law, any capital
35 improvement that may be leased by the authority to the stadium
36 board under this chapter may also be leased by the authority to
37 any state agency to accomplish the purposes of this chapter. Any
38 lease between the authority and a state agency under this chapter:
39 (1) must set forth the terms and conditions of the use and
40 occupancy under the lease;
41 (2) must set forth the amounts agreed to be paid at stated
42 intervals for the use and occupancy under the lease;
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

15
1 (3) must provide that the state agency is not obligated to
2 continue to pay for the use and occupancy under the lease but
3 is instead required to vacate the facility if it is shown that the
4 terms and conditions of the use and occupancy and the
5 amount to be paid for the use and occupancy are unjust and
6 unreasonable considering the value of the services and
7 facilities thereby afforded;
8 (4) must provide that the state agency is required to vacate
9 the facility if funds have not been appropriated or are not
10 available to pay any sum agreed to be paid for use and
11 occupancy when due;
12 (5) may provide for such costs as maintenance, operations,
13 taxes, and insurance to be paid by the state agency;
14 (6) may contain an option to renew the lease;
15 (7) may contain an option to purchase the facility for an
16 amount equal to the amount required to pay the principal and
17 interest of indebtedness of the authority incurred on account
18 of the facility and expenses of the authority attributable to the
19 facility;
20 (8) may provide for payment of sums for use and occupancy
21 of an existing capital improvement being used by the state
22 agency, but may not provide for payment of sums for use and
23 occupancy of a new capital improvement until the
24 construction of the capital improvement or portion thereof
25 has been completed and the new capital improvement or a
26 portion thereof is available for use and occupancy by the state
27 agency; and
28 (9) may contain any other provisions agreeable to the
29 authority and the state agency.
30 (b) Any state agency that leases a capital improvement from the
31 authority under this chapter may sublease the capital improvement
32 to the stadium board under the terms and conditions set forth in
33 section 13(a) of this chapter, section 13(b)(1) through 13(b)(4) of
34 this chapter, section 13(b)(6) through 13(b)(8) of this chapter, and
35 section 13(c) of this chapter.
36 (c) Notwithstanding any other law, in anticipation of the

40 agency and then lease the facility to the state agency. A lease made
41 under this subsection shall describe the capital improvement to be
42 constructed and may provide for the payment of rent by the state
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

16
1 agency for the use of the existing facility. If such rent is to be paid

8 fiscal body adopts such an ordinance, the clerk shall immediately
9 send a certified copy of the ordinance to the commissioner of the
10 department of state revenue.
11 (c) A tax imposed under this chapter terminates on January 1
12 of the year immediately following the year in which the last
13 payment obligation of the board is made with respect to any bond,
14 lease, or other obligation described in section 8(a) of this chapter.

32 Chapter 78. Hammond Admissions Tax
33 Sec. 1. This chapter applies to the city of Hammond.
34 Sec. 2. (a) The fiscal body of the city may adopt an ordinance to
35 impose an excise tax, known as the city admissions tax, for the
36 privilege of attending any event:
37 (1) held in a facility located within the boundaries of the city
38 and that has a seating capacity of more than forty thousand
39 (40,000); and
40 (2) to which tickets are offered for sale to the public by:
41 (A) the box office of the facility; or
42 (B) an authorized agent of the facility.
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

26
1 (b) For purposes of this section, the sale, license, purchase, or

4 seat license, does not constitute a taxable event and is not subject
5 to the city admissions tax, the state gross retail tax under
6 IC 6-2.5-2, or the state use tax under IC 6-2.5-3.
7 (c) If the fiscal body of the city adopts an ordinance under
8 subsection (a), it shall immediately send a certified copy of the
9 ordinance to the commissioner of the department of state revenue.
10 (d) If the fiscal body of the city adopts an ordinance under
11 subsection (a) prior to June 1, the city admissions tax applies to

13 ordinance is adopted. If the fiscal body of the city adopts an
14 ordinance under subsection (a) of this chapter on or after June 1,
15 the city admissions tax applies to admission charges collected after
16 the last day of the month in which the ordinance is adopted.

30 ordinance is adopted.

23 Chapter 31.6. Northwest Indiana Professional Sports
24 Development Area
25 Sec. 1. The following definitions apply throughout this chapter:
26 (1) "Authority" means the northwest Indiana stadium
27 authority created by IC 5-1-17.1.
28 (2) "Board" refers to the northwest Indiana stadium board
29 created by IC 36-10-9.5.
30 (3) "Bonds" means bonds, notes, or other evidence of
31 indebtedness.
32 (4) "Budget agency" means the budget agency created by
33 IC 4-12-1.
34 (5) "Budget committee" means the budget committee
35 established by IC 4-12-1-3.
36 (6) "Capital improvement" means any facility or complex of
37 facilities established as part of the professional sports
38 development area under section 3 of this chapter.
39 (7) "City" refers to the city of Hammond, Indiana.
40 (8) "Commission" means a redevelopment commission of the
41 city.
42 (9) "Covered taxes" means the following:
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

34
1 (A) The state gross retail tax imposed under IC 6-2.5-2-1
2 or use tax imposed under IC 6-2.5-3-2.
3 (B) An adjusted gross income tax imposed under
4 IC 6-3-2-1 on an individual.
5 (C) The local income tax imposed under IC 6-3.6.
6 (D) A food and beverage tax imposed under IC 6-9-36 or
7 IC 6-9-58.
8 (10) "Department" refers to the department of state revenue.
9 (11) "Facility" means all or any part of one (1) or more
10 buildings, structures, or improvements constituting a capital
11 improvement. The term refers to and includes a capital
12 improvement.
13 (12) "Tax area" means the geographic area established as the
14 professional sports development area under section 3 of this
15 chapter.
16 (13) "Taxpayer" means a person that is liable for a covered
17 tax.
18 Sec. 2. (a) The general assembly finds the following:
19 (1) Northwest Indiana, including the city, faces unique and
20 distinct challenges and opportunities related to economic
21 development issues associated with the construction of
22 facilities that would host professional sporting and
23 entertainment events in the city.
24 (2) A unique approach is required to ensure that the facilities
25 can be maintained to allow northwest Indiana to meet these
26 challenges and opportunities.
27 (3) The powers and responsibilities provided to the city, the
28 authority, and the board by this chapter are appropriate and
29 necessary to carry out the public purposes of encouraging and
30 fostering economic development in northwest Indiana and
31 constructing facilities that would host professional sporting
32 and entertainment events in the city.
33 (4) Encouragement of economic development in Indiana will:
34 (A) generate significant economic activity, which may
35 attract new businesses and encourage existing businesses
36 to remain or expand in northwest Indiana;
37 (B) promote northwest Indiana to residents outside
38 Indiana, which may attract residents outside Indiana and
39 new businesses to relocate to northwest Indiana;
40 (C) protect and increase state and local tax revenues; and
41 (D) encourage overall economic growth in northwest
42 Indiana and in Indiana.
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

35
1 (b) Northwest Indiana faces unique challenges in the
2 development of infrastructure and other facilities necessary to
3 promote economic development:
4 (1) as a result of its need to rely on sources of revenue other
5 than property taxes;
6 (2) due to the large number of tax exempt properties located
7 in northwest Indiana; and
8 (3) because northwest Indiana is the site of numerous state
9 and regional nonprofit corporations.
10 (c) Economic development benefits the health and welfare of the
11 people of Indiana, is a public use and purpose for which public
12 money may be spent, and is of public utility and benefit.
13 Sec. 3. (a) A commission may establish a professional sports
14 development area in the city designated as the "northwest Indiana
15 professional sports development area".
16 (b) The commission may establish as part of the professional
17 sports development area any facility or complex of facilities that is:
18 (1) used to hold a professional sporting event, including a
19 stadium, and which in addition, may be used to hold other
20 entertainment events, including any publicly owned parking,
21 including any public parking garages, plaza, or infrastructure
22 that is constructed or renovated in connection with the
23 construction of the facility used to hold a professional
24 sporting event;
25 (2) used in the training of a team engaged in professional
26 sporting events; and
27 (3) used in whole or in part to manage and operate the
28 professional team that would participate in the facility used to
29 hold a professional sporting event.
30 The tax area shall include any facility described in this subsection
31 and any parcel of land on which the facility is located. An area may
32 contain noncontiguous tracts of land within the city.
33 (c) Only the facilities described in subsection (b) that are
34 included within the professional sports development area may be
35 financed with debt issued by the board, the authority, or a political
36 subdivision.
37 Sec. 4. (a) A tax area must be initially established not later than
38 July 1, 2027, according to the procedures set forth for the
39 establishment of an economic development area under IC 36-7-14.
40 A tax area may be changed or the terms governing the tax area
41 revised in the same manner as the establishment of the initial tax
42 area.
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

36
1 (b) In establishing or changing the terms of the tax area or
2 revising the terms governing the tax area, the commission must
3 make the following findings required for the establishment of
4 economic development areas:
5 (1) That a project to be undertaken or that has been
6 undertaken in the tax area is for a facility.
7 (2) That the project to be undertaken or that has been
8 undertaken in the tax area will benefit the public health and
9 welfare and will be of public utility and benefit.
10 (3) That the project to be undertaken or that has been
11 undertaken in the tax area will protect or increase state and
12 local tax bases and tax revenues.
13 (c) The tax area established by the commission under this
14 chapter is a special taxing district authorized by the general
15 assembly to enable the authority and the board to provide special
16 benefits to taxpayers in the tax area by promoting economic
17 development that is of public use and benefit.

21 (1) publish notice of the adoption and substance of the

42 the budget agency must make the following findings:
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

37
1 (1) The project specified in the resolution is economically
2 sound and will benefit the people of Indiana by protecting or

4 Sec. 7. (a) A tax area must be established by resolution. A
5 resolution establishing a tax area may provide for the allocation of
6 covered taxes attributable to a taxable event or covered taxes
7 earned in the tax area to the professional sports development area
8 fund established for the city. The allocation provision must apply
9 to the part of the tax area covered by this section. The resolution
10 must provide that the tax area terminates not later than forty (40)
11 years from the date the first obligation payable from covered taxes
12 is incurred by the board. Covered taxes may not be collected in the
13 tax area until after the earlier of June 30, 2027, or the date on
14 which all the conditions set forth in this chapter are met. Any
15 covered taxes attributable to a taxable event or covered taxes
16 earned in the tax area shall be allocated to the professional sports
17 development area fund established for the board.
18 (b) All of the salary, wages, bonuses, and other compensation

22 (2) taxable in Indiana; and
23 (3) earned in the tax area;
24 shall be allocated to the tax area if the professional athlete is a

26 in the tax area.
27 (c) The resolution establishing the tax area must designate the

5 SECTION 27. IC 36-7-32.6 IS ADDED TO THE INDIANA CODE
6 AS A NEW CHAPTER TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
7 UPON PASSAGE]:
8 Chapter 32.6. Northwest Indiana Stadium Development District
9 Sec. 1. As used in this chapter, "base assessed value" means the
10 net assessed value of all the taxable real property that is assessed
11 as commercial, residential, or industrial property under the rules
12 of the department of local government finance, and taxable
13 personal property that is located in the stadium development
14 district as finally determined for the assessment date immediately
15 preceding the effective date of the designation by the city under
16 section 14 of this chapter.
17 Sec. 2. As used in this chapter, "board" refers to the northwest
18 Indiana stadium board created by IC 36-10-9.5.
19 Sec. 3. As used in this chapter, "city" means the city of
20 Hammond, Indiana.
21 Sec. 4. As used in this chapter, "contractor" has the meaning set
22 forth in IC 6-2.5-1-14.9.
23 Sec. 5. As used in this chapter, "designating body" means the
24 legislative body of the city.
25 Sec. 6. As used in this chapter, "executive" means the executive
26 of the city.
27 Sec. 7. As used in this chapter, "gross retail base period
28 amount" means the aggregate amount of state gross retail and use
29 taxes remitted under IC 6-2.5:
30 (1) by the businesses operating in the territory comprising the
31 stadium development district; and
32 (2) that is, in the case of the:
33 (A) state gross retail tax, collected by a business for sales
34 occurring at a physical location of the business in the
35 stadium development district;
36 (B) state use tax, incurred with regard to property used in
37 the stadium development district; and
38 (C) state gross retail and use tax incurred and paid by a
39 contractor with regard to tangible personal property
40 incorporated into real property that is located in the
41 stadium development district, if the:
42 (i) contractor can determine the amount of state gross
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

42
1 retail or use tax incurred and paid on the tangible
2 personal property incorporated into real property that
3 is located in the stadium development district based on
4 records maintained under section 24 of this chapter; and
5 (ii) state gross retail or use tax is not otherwise included
6 in the stadium development district or section 8 of this
7 chapter;
8 during the full state fiscal year that precedes the date on which the
9 stadium development district was designated under section 14 of
10 this chapter.
11 Sec. 8. As used in this chapter, "gross retail incremental
12 amount" means the remainder of:
13 (1) the aggregate amount of state gross retail and use taxes
14 that are remitted under IC 6-2.5:
15 (A) by businesses operating in the territory comprising the
16 stadium development district; and
17 (B) that is, in the case of the:
18 (i) state gross retail tax, collected by a business for sales
19 occurring at a physical location of the business in the
20 stadium development district;
21 (ii) state use tax, incurred with regard to property used
22 in the stadium development district; and
23 (iii) state gross retail and use tax incurred and paid by a
24 contractor with regard to tangible personal property
25 incorporated into real property that is located in the
26 stadium development district, if the contractor can
27 determine the amount of state gross retail or use tax
28 incurred and paid based on records maintained under
29 section 24 of this chapter and the state gross retail and
30 use tax is not otherwise included in the stadium
31 development district or section 7 of this chapter;
32 during the state fiscal year; minus
33 (2) the gross retail base period amount;
34 as determined by the department of state revenue.
35 Sec. 9. As used in this chapter, "income tax base period
36 amount" means the aggregate amount of state adjusted gross
37 income taxes paid:
38 (1) by employees employed in the territory comprising the
39 stadium development district with respect to wages and salary
40 earned for work in the stadium development district; and
41 (2) by individuals who are not employees with respect to
42 income received for services performed in the territory
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

43
1 comprising the stadium development district;
2 for the state fiscal year that precedes the date on which the stadium
3 development district is designated under section 14 of this chapter.
4 Sec. 10. As used in this chapter, "income tax incremental
5 amount" means the remainder of:
6 (1) the total amount of state adjusted gross income taxes paid:
7 (A) by employees employed in the territory comprising the
8 stadium development district with respect to wages and
9 salary earned for work in the territory comprising the
10 stadium development district; and
11 (B) by individuals who are not employees with respect to
12 income received for services performed in the territory
13 comprising the stadium development district;
14 for a particular state fiscal year; minus
15 (2) the income tax base period amount.
16 Sec. 11. As used in this chapter, "net increment" means the sum
17 of:
18 (1) the gross retail incremental amount; plus
19 (2) the income tax incremental amount;
20 as determined by the department of state revenue.
21 Sec. 12. As used in this chapter. "professional sports
22 development area" means the northwest Indiana professional
23 sports development area that may be established under
24 IC 36-7-31.6.
25 Sec. 13. As used in this chapter, "stadium development district"
26 means the northwest Indiana stadium development district that
27 may be established under this chapter.
28 Sec. 14. The designating body may, by resolution or ordinance
29 adopted by the designating body, designate a stadium development
30 district in the city. Any such resolution or ordinance adopted by
31 the designating body shall include:
32 (1) a description of the stadium development district;
33 (2) the term of the stadium development district; and
34 (3) the plan for the stadium development district which shall
35 conform to the requirements of section 18 of chapter.
36 The boundaries of the stadium development district may not
37 extend beyond the corporate boundaries of the city and may not
38 include any territory that is within the professional sports
39 development area. The designating body may not designate any
40 more than one (1) stadium development district in the city.

42 a stadium development district under section 14 of this chapter, the
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

44
1 designating body shall submit the resolution or ordinance to the

5 otherwise applies to territory within the stadium development
6 district.

8 designated in section 14 of this chapter may not exceed thirty-five

10 reviews the resolution or ordinance designating a stadium
11 development district pursuant to section 15 of this chapter.

36 Chapter 9.5. Northwest Indiana Stadium Board
37 Sec. 1. As used in this chapter:
38 "Board" refers to a northwest Indiana stadium board created
39 under this chapter.
40 "Bonds" means bonds issued under section 12 or 15 of this
41 chapter and, except as used in section 12 of this chapter or
42 unless the context otherwise requires, lease agreements
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

54
1 entered into under section 5(15) of this chapter.
2 "Capital improvement" means the building, facilities, or
3 improvements that the board determines will be of general
4 public benefit or welfare and will promote the cultural,
5 recreational, public, or civic well-being of the city and
6 northwest Indiana. This includes the land comprising the site,
7 equipment, heating and air conditioning facilities, sewage
8 disposal facilities, landscaping, walks, drives, parking
9 facilities, and other structures, facilities, appurtenances,
10 materials, equipment, and supplies that are necessary to make
11 any building, facility, or improvement suitable for the use for
12 which it was constructed.
13 "City" means the city of Hammond, Indiana.
14 "Contract" includes a lease or other agreement.
15 "Controller" means the controller appointed by the board
16 pursuant to section 8(c) of this chapter.
17 "County" means, collectively, Lake and Porter counties.
18 "Excise taxes" refers to the excise taxes imposed by IC 6-9-36,
19 IC 6-9-58, and IC 6-9-78.
20 "Issue", "issued", or "issuance" means in the case of lease
21 agreements "execute", "executed", or "execution",
22 respectively.
23 "Lease agreements" means lease agreements entered into
24 under section 5(15) of this chapter.
25 "Net income" means the gross income from the operation of
26 a capital improvement after deducting the necessary
27 operating expenses of the board.
28 "Notes" means notes issued under section 20 of this chapter.
29 "Operating expenses" means:
30 (A) the necessary operational expenses of the board in
31 performing its duties under this chapter, including
32 maintenance, repairs, replacements, alterations, and costs
33 of services of architects, engineers, accountants, attorneys,
34 and consultants;
35 (B) the expenses for any other purpose that has been
36 approved under section 7 of this chapter; and
37 (C) the maintenance of reasonable reserves for any of the
38 items listed in clauses (A) and (B) of this definition or for
39 other purposes required under a resolution, ordinance, or
40 trust agreement.
41 "Principal and interest" or "principal on and interest of"
42 includes, unless the context otherwise requires, payments
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

55
1 required by lease agreements.
2 "Project" refers to a project of the board for the construction
3 or lease of a facility and all buildings, facilities, structures,
4 and improvements related to that facility.
5 "Public benefit" refers to a grant, a tax abatement, a tax
6 credit, or establishment or use of tax area revenues related to
7 a project.
8 "Public finance director" means the public finance director
9 appointed under IC 5-1.2-3-6.
10 "Trust agreements", except as used in section 13 of this
11 chapter or unless the context otherwise requires, includes
12 lease agreements.
13 Sec. 2. (a) A northwest Indiana stadium board is hereby created.
14 (b) The northwest Indiana stadium board may finance,
15 construct, equip, operate, and maintain a capital improvement
16 under this chapter.
17 Sec. 3. (a) The board is composed of the following five (5)
18 members:
19 (1) The director of the office of management and budget, or
20 the director's designee, who shall serve as president of the
21 board.
22 (2) Two (2) members appointed by the executive of the city.
23 (3) The public finance director, or the director's designee.
24 (4) One (1) member selected by the public finance director.
25 (b) A member appointed under subsection (a)(2) serves an initial
26 term that expires December 31, 2027, and each fourth year
27 thereafter. The member may be reappointed by the appointing
28 authority to subsequent terms.
29 (c) A member appointed under subsection (a)(4) serves an initial
30 term that expires December 31, 2028, and each fourth year
31 thereafter. The member may be reappointed by the public finance
32 director to subsequent terms.
33 (d) If a vacancy occurs on the board, the appointing authority
34 shall appoint a new member. That member serves for the
35 remainder of the vacated term.
36 (e) A member may be removed for cause by the appointing
37 authority who appointed the member.
38 (f) Each member, before entering upon the duties of office, shall
39 take and subscribe an oath of office in the usual form. The oath
40 shall be endorsed upon the member's certificate of appointment,
41 which shall be promptly filed with the records of the board.
42 (g) A member does not receive a salary, but is entitled to
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

56
1 reimbursement for any expenses necessarily incurred in the
2 performance of the member's duties.
3 Sec. 4. (a) The board shall hold an annual organizational
4 meeting. It shall elect one (1) of the members vice president,
5 another secretary, and another treasurer to perform the duties of
6 those offices. The officers serve from the date of their election until
7 their successors are elected and qualified.
8 (b) Special meetings may be called by the president of the board.
9 (c) The board may adopt the bylaws and rules that it considers
10 necessary for the proper conduct of its duties and the safeguarding
11 of the funds and property entrusted to its care. A majority of the
12 members constitutes a quorum, and the concurrence of a majority
13 of the members is necessary to authorize any action.
14 (d) Subject to IC 5-14-1.5-3.6, members of the board may
15 participate in a meeting of the board by electronic communication.
16 Sec. 5. The board may, acting under the title "northwest
17 Indiana stadium board", do the following:
18 (1) Acquire by grant, purchase, gift, devise, lease,
19 condemnation, or otherwise, and hold, use, sell, lease, or
20 dispose of, real and personal property and all property rights
21 and interests necessary or convenient for the exercise of its
22 powers under this chapter.
23 (2) Construct, reconstruct, repair, remodel, enlarge, extend,
24 or add to any capital improvement built or acquired by the
25 board under this chapter.
26 (3) Control and operate a capital improvement, including
27 letting concessions and leasing all or part of the capital
28 improvement.
29 (4) Fix charges and establish rules governing the use of a
30 capital improvement.
31 (5) Accept gifts or contributions from individuals,
32 corporations, limited liability companies, partnerships,
33 associations, trusts, or political subdivisions, foundations, and
34 funds, loans, or advances on the terms that the board
35 considers necessary or desirable from the United States, the
36 state, and any political subdivision or department of either,
37 including entering into and carrying out contracts and
38 agreements in connection with this subdivision.
39 (6) Exercise in the name of the board the power of eminent
40 domain under general statutes governing the exercise of the
41 power for a public purpose.
42 (7) Receive and collect money due for the use or leasing of a
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

57
1 capital improvement and from concessions and other
2 contracts, and expend the money for proper purposes.
3 (8) Receive excise taxes, income taxes, ad valorem property
4 taxes, and any other taxes or revenues and expend the money
5 for operating expenses, payments of principal or interest of
6 bonds or notes issued under this chapter, and for all or part
7 of the cost of a capital improvement.
8 (9) Retain the services of architects, engineers, accountants,
9 attorneys, and consultants and hire employees upon terms
10 and conditions established by the board, so long as any
11 employees or members of the board authorized to receive,
12 collect, and expend money are covered by a fidelity bond, the
13 amount of which shall be fixed by the board. Funds may not
14 be disbursed by an employee or member of the board without
15 prior specific approval by the board.
16 (10) Provide coverage for its employees under IC 22-3 and
17 IC 22-4.
18 (11) Purchase public liability and other insurance considered
19 desirable.
20 (12) Make and enter into all leases, contracts, and agreements
21 necessary or incidental to the performance of its duties and
22 the execution of its powers under this chapter, including the
23 enforcement of them.
24 (13) Sue and be sued in the name and style of "northwest
25 Indiana stadium board", service of process being had by
26 leaving a copy at the board's office.
27 (14) Prepare and publish descriptive material and literature
28 relating to the facilities and advantages of a capital
29 improvement and do all other acts that the board considers
30 necessary to promote and publicize the capital improvement,
31 including the convention and visitor industry, and serve the
32 commercial, industrial, and cultural interests of Indiana and
33 its citizens. The board may assist, cooperate, and fund
34 governmental, public, and private agencies and groups for
35 these purposes.
36 (15) Enter into leases of capital improvements and sell or lease
37 property under IC 5-1-17.1.
38 Sec. 6. (a) The purchase or lease of material and work on a
39 capital improvement shall be done by the board under statutes
40 governing these activities by counties. However, if the total cost of
41 construction or equipping of a capital improvement or of the
42 alteration, maintenance, or repair of any building is estimated to
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

58
1 be fifty thousand dollars ($50,000) or less, the board may procure
2 materials and perform the work by its own employees and with
3 owned or leased equipment without awarding a contract. In
4 addition, in an emergency determined and declared by the board
5 and entered in its records, the board may make emergency
6 alterations, repairs, or replacements and contract for them without
7 advertising for bids.
8 (b) Title to or interest in any property acquired shall be held in
9 the name of the board, and the board has complete and exclusive
10 authority to sell, lease, or dispose of it and to execute all
11 conveyances, leases, contracts, and other instruments in connection
12 with it.
13 Sec. 7. (a) The board shall prepare a budget for each calendar
14 year covering the projected operating expenses, projected
15 expenditures for capital improvements or land acquisition, and
16 estimated income to pay the operating expenses and capital
17 expenditures, including amounts, if any, to be received from excise
18 taxes, ad valorem property taxes, and any other taxes or revenues.
19 It shall submit the operating and capital budget for review,
20 approval, or rejection to the public finance director. The board
21 may make expenditures only as provided in the budget as
22 approved, unless additional expenditures are approved by the
23 public finance director. However, payments to users of any capital
24 improvement that constitute a contractual share of box office
25 receipts are neither an operating expense nor an expenditure
26 within the meaning of this section.
27 (b) If the board desires to finance a capital improvement in
28 whole or in part by the issuance of bonds under section 12 or 15 of
29 this chapter, the board shall submit the following information to
30 the northwest Indiana stadium authority at least thirty (30) days
31 before the adoption of a resolution authorizing the issuance of the
32 bonds:
33 (1) A description of the project to be financed through the
34 issuance of bonds.
35 (2) The total amount of the project anticipated to be funded
36 through the issuance of bonds.
37 (3) The total amount of other anticipated revenue sources for
38 the project.
39 (4) Any other terms upon which the bonds will be issued.
40 (c) The northwest Indiana stadium authority must discuss the
41 information provided in subsection (b) in a public hearing held
42 before the resolution may be adopted by the board.

3 Sec. 8. (a) The treasurer of the board is the official custodian of
4 all funds and assets of the board and is responsible for their
5 safeguarding and accounting. The treasurer shall give bond for the

19 reinvested by the treasurer in accordance with general statutes
20 relating to the investment of public funds and in securities that the
21 board specifically directs. All interest and other income earned on
22 investments becomes a part of the particular fund from which the
23 money was invested, except as provided in a resolution, ordinance,
24 or trust agreement providing for the issuance of bonds or notes. All
25 funds invested in deposit accounts as provided in IC 5-13-9 must be
26 insured under IC 5-13-12.
27 (c) The board shall appoint a controller to act as the auditor and
28 assistant treasurer of the board. The controller shall serve as the
29 official custodian of all books of account and other financial
30 records of the board and has the same powers and duties as the
31 treasurer of the board or the lesser powers and duties that the
32 board prescribes. The controller and any other employee or
33 member of the board authorized to receive, collect, or expend
34 money shall give bond for the faithful performance and discharge
35 of all duties required of the controller in the amount and with
36 surety and other conditions that may be prescribed and approved
37 by the board. The controller shall keep an accurate account of all
38 money due the board and of all money received, invested, and
39 disbursed in accordance with generally recognized governmental
40 accounting principles and procedure. All accounting forms and
41 records shall be prescribed or approved by the state board of
42 accounts.

14 manual or facsimile signature of the president of the board, and
15 attested by the manual or facsimile signature of the treasurer of
16 the board. However, one (1) of the signatures must be manual,
17 unless the bonds are authenticated by the manual signature of an
18 authorized officer or a trustee for the bondholders. Any coupons
19 attached must bear the facsimile signature of the president of the
20 board.
21 (h) This chapter constitutes full and complete authority for the
22 issuance of revenue bonds. No law, procedure, proceedings,
23 publications, notices, consents, approvals, orders, acts, or things by
24 the board or any other officer, department, agency, or
25 instrumentality of the state or any political subdivision is required
26 to issue any revenue bonds except as prescribed in this chapter.
27 (i) Revenue bonds issued under this section are legal investments
28 for private trust funds and the funds of banks, trust companies,
29 insurance companies, building and loan associations, credit unions,
30 banks of discount and deposit, savings banks, loan and trust and
31 safe deposit companies, rural loan and savings associations,
32 guaranty loan and savings associations, mortgage guaranty
33 companies, small loan companies, industrial loan and investment
34 companies, and other financial institutions organized under
35 statute.
36 Sec. 13. (a) Revenue bonds issued under this chapter may be
37 secured by a trust agreement by and between the board and a
38 corporate trustee, which may be any trust company or bank having
39 the powers of a trust company in Indiana. Any resolution adopted
40 by the board providing for the issuance of revenue bonds and any
41 trust agreement under which the revenue bonds are issued may
42 pledge or assign, subject only to valid prior pledges, all or a part of
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

66
1 the amounts authorized by this chapter, but the board may not
2 convey or mortgage any capital improvement or any part of a
3 capital improvement.
4 (b) In authorizing the issuance of revenue bonds, the board
5 may:
6 (1) limit the amount of revenue bonds that may be issued as a
7 first lien against the amounts pledged to the payment of those
8 revenue bonds; or
9 (2) authorize the issuance from time to time of additional
10 revenue bonds secured by the same lien.
11 Additional revenue bonds shall be issued on the terms and
12 conditions provided in the bond resolution or resolutions adopted
13 by the board and in the trust agreement or any agreement
14 supplemental to the trust agreement. Additional revenue bonds
15 may be secured equally and ratably without preference, priority,
16 or distinction with the original issue of revenue bonds or may be
17 made junior to the original issue of revenue bonds.
18 (c) Any pledge or assignment made by the board under this
19 section is valid and binding from the time that the pledge or
20 assignment is made, and the amounts pledged and received by the
21 board are immediately subject to the lien of the pledge or
22 assignment without physical delivery of those amounts or further
23 act. The lien of the pledge or assignment is valid and binding
24 against all parties having claims of any kind in tort, contract, or
25 otherwise against the board irrespective of whether these parties
26 have notice of the lien. Neither the resolution nor any trust
27 agreement by which a pledge is created or an assignment need be
28 filed or recorded in order to perfect the resulting lien against third
29 parties. However, a copy of the pledge or assignment shall be filed
30 in the records of the board.
31 (d) Any trust agreement or resolution providing for the issuance
32 of revenue bonds may contain provisions for protecting and
33 enforcing the rights and remedies of the bondholders that are
34 reasonable and proper and not in violation of law. The provisions
35 may include covenants stating the duties of the board in relation to:
36 (1) the acquisition of property;
37 (2) the construction, improvement, maintenance, repair,
38 operation, and insurance of the capital improvement or
39 capital improvements in connection with which the bonds
40 have been authorized;
41 (3) the rates of fees, rentals, or other charges to be collected
42 for the use of the capital improvement or capital
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

67
1 improvements;
2 (4) the custody, safeguarding, investment, and application of
3 all money received or to be received by the board or trustee;
4 (5) the establishment of funds, reserves, and accounts; and
5 (6) the employment of consulting engineers in connection with
6 the construction or operation of the capital improvement or
7 capital improvements.
8 (e) It is lawful for any bank or trust company incorporated
9 under statute, and any national banking association that may act
10 as depository of the proceeds of bonds or other funds of the board,
11 to furnish indemnifying bonds or to pledge securities that are
12 required by the board.
13 (f) Any trust agreement entered into under this section may
14 state the rights and remedies of the bondholders and of the trustee,
15 and may restrict the individual right of action by bondholders as
16 is customary in trust agreements or trust indentures securing
17 bonds or debentures of private corporations. In addition, the trust
18 agreement may contain other provisions that the board considers
19 reasonable and proper for the security of the bondholders.
20 (g) All expenses incurred in carrying out a trust agreement
21 entered into under this section may be treated as a part of the
22 necessary operating expenses of the board.
23 Sec. 14. (a) The Indiana general assembly covenants with the
24 purchasers of any bonds or notes issued under this chapter that:
25 (1) the excise taxes pledged to the payment of those bonds and
26 notes will not be repealed, amended, or altered in any manner
27 that would reduce or adversely affect the levy and collection
28 of those taxes; and
29 (2) it will not reduce the rates or amounts of those taxes; as
30 long as the principal of, or interest on, any bonds or notes is
31 unpaid.
32 (b) The board may make a similar pledge or covenant in any
33 agreement with the purchasers of any bonds or notes issued under
34 this chapter.
35 (c) For purposes of this section, the principal of or interest on
36 bonds or notes is considered paid if provision has been made for
37 their payment in such a manner that the bonds or notes are not
38 considered to be outstanding under the resolution, ordinance, or
39 trust agreement under which the bonds or notes are issued.
40 Sec. 15. (a) A capital improvement may be financed in whole or
41 in part by the issuance of general obligation bonds of the city.
42 (b) If the board desires to finance a capital improvement in

1 whole or in part as provided in this section, it shall have prepared

1 or at a negotiated sale;

3 Sec. 16. All money received from any bonds issued under this
4 chapter shall be applied solely to the payment of the construction
5 cost of the capital improvement or capital improvements or the
6 cost of refunding or refinancing outstanding bonds or notes, for
7 which the bonds are issued. The cost may include:
8 (1) planning and development of the capital improvement and
9 all buildings, facilities, structures, and improvements related
10 to it;
11 (2) acquisition of a site and clearing and preparing the site for
12 construction;
13 (3) equipment, facilities, structures, and improvements that
14 are necessary or desirable to make the capital improvement
15 suitable for use and operation;
16 (4) architectural, engineering, consultant, and attorney's fees;
17 (5) incidental expenses in connection with the issuance and
18 sale of bonds;
19 (6) reserves for principal and interest and for operations,
20 extensions, replacements, renovations, and improvements;
21 (7) interest during construction;
22 (8) financial advisory fees;
23 (9) insurance during construction;
24 (10) municipal bond insurance; and
25 (11) in the case of refunding or refinancing, payment of the
26 principal of, redemption premiums, if any, for, and interest on
27 the bonds or notes being refunded or refinanced.
28 Sec. 17. Unless their rights are restricted by the appropriate
29 bond resolution, ordinance, or trust agreement, any holder of notes
30 or bonds issued under this chapter or a trustee under a trust
31 agreement entered into under this chapter may, by any suitable
32 form of legal proceeding, protect and enforce any rights provided
33 under statute or granted by the bond resolution, ordinance, or
34 trust agreement.
35 Sec. 18. All:
36 (1) property owned by the board;
37 (2) property leased to or by the board; and
38 (3) income and revenues received by the board;
39 are exempt from special assessments and taxation in Indiana for all
40 purposes.
41 Sec. 19. The board and the state, any department, agency, or
42 commission of the state, or any department, agency, or commission
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

70
1 of municipal or county government, may enter into agreements,
2 contracts, or leases with each other on the terms that are agreed
3 upon, providing for joint and cooperative planning, financing,
4 construction, operation, or maintenance of a capital improvement
5 or of the buildings, facilities, structures, or improvements that are
6 necessary or desirable in connection with the use and operation of
7 a capital improvement.
8 Sec. 20. (a) In anticipation of funds to be received from any
9 source, the board may borrow money and issue notes for a term
10 not exceeding ten (10) years and at a rate or rates of interest
11 determined by the board. The notes shall be issued in the name of
12 the "northwest Indiana stadium board" and may be secured
13 (either on a parity with or junior and subordinate to any
14 outstanding bonds or notes) by:
15 (1) the pledge of income and revenues of any capital
16 improvement;
17 (2) the proceeds of excise taxes; or
18 (3) any other funds anticipated to be received.
19 The notes are payable solely from the income, excise taxes,
20 revenues, and anticipated funds.
21 (b) The financing may be negotiated directly by the board with
22 any bank, insurance company, savings association, or other
23 financial institution licensed to do business in Indiana upon the
24 terms and conditions that are agreed upon, except as specifically
25 provided in this section, and may be consummated without public
26 offering. The notes plus interest are exempt from taxation in
27 Indiana as provided for bonds in IC 6-8-5.
28 Sec. 21. A board established under this chapter may defend any
29 current or former member of the board or its officers, employees,
30 or agents in a claim or suit, at law or in equity, that arises from the
31 exercise of powers or the performance of duties or services for the
32 board or that arises from official acts as a member of the board.
33 The board may indemnify a person for any liability, cost, or
34 damages related to a claim or suit, including the payment of legal
35 fees. Before taking action authorized by this section, the board
36 must, by resolution, determine that the action or conduct in
37 question was taken, done, or omitted in good faith.
38 SECTION 30. An emergency is declared for this act.

"Sec. 0.3. The general assembly finds the following:
(1) Northwest Indiana as a region and the city face unique and
distinct challenges and opportunities related to the economic
development issues associated with the construction and
maintenance of a world-class stadium facility in the city.
(2) A unique approach is required to ensure that northwest
Indiana has sufficient revenue sources to allow it to meet these
challenges and opportunities.
(3) The powers and responsibilities provided to northwest
Indiana and to the northwest Indiana stadium authority
created by this chapter are appropriate and necessary to
carry out the public purposes of encouraging and fostering
economic development in northwest Indiana and constructing
a world-class stadium facility in the city.
(4) The relocation of a National Football League franchised
professional football team in northwest Indiana poses unique
challenges due to the need for development of a world-class
football stadium and related infrastructure that would not be
needed apart from the needs related to the relocation of a
National Football League franchised professional football
team in the city.
(5) The relocation of a National Football League franchised
professional football team in the city is critical to successful
economic development in the city and northwest Indiana and
is a public purpose.
(6) Encouragement of economic development in northwest
Indiana will:
(A) provide significant economic activity, a substantial
portion of which results from persons residing outside
Indiana, which may attract new businesses and encourage
existing businesses to remain or expand in the city and
northwest Indiana;
(B) promote the city and northwest Indiana to residents
outside Indiana, which may attract residents outside
Indiana and new businesses to relocate to the city and
northwest Indiana area;
(C) protect and increase state and local tax revenues; and

(7) Northwest Indiana faces unique challenges in the

(B) due to the large number of tax exempt properties
located in northwest Indiana; and

and regional nonprofit corporations.
(8) Economic development benefits the health and welfare of
the people of Indiana, is a public use and purpose for which

SECTION 20. IC 6-9-78 IS ADDED TO THE INDIANA CODE AS
A NEW CHAPTER TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE UPON
PASSAGE]:
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

87
Chapter 78. Hammond Admissions Tax
Sec. 1. This chapter applies to the city of Hammond.
Sec. 2. (a) The fiscal body of the city may adopt an ordinance to
impose an excise tax, known as the city admissions tax, for the
privilege of attending any event:
(1) held in a facility located within the boundaries of the city
and that has a seating capacity of more than forty thousand
(40,000); and
(2) to which tickets are offered for sale to the public by:
(A) the box office of the facility; or
(B) an authorized agent of the facility.
(b) For purposes of this section, the sale, license, purchase, or
transfer of a contractual right to purchase season tickets for a
professional sporting event, commonly referred to as a personal
seat license, does not constitute a taxable event and is not subject
to the city admissions tax, the state gross retail tax under
IC 6-2.5-2, or the state use tax under IC 6-2.5-3.
(c) If the fiscal body of the city adopts an ordinance under
subsection (a), it shall immediately send a certified copy of the
ordinance to the commissioner of the department of state revenue.
(d) If the fiscal body of the city adopts an ordinance under
subsection (a) prior to June 1, the city admissions tax applies to
admission charges collected after June 30 of the year in which the
ordinance is adopted. If the fiscal body of the city adopts an
ordinance under subsection (a) of this chapter on or after June 1,
the city admissions tax applies to admission charges collected after
the last day of the month in which the ordinance is adopted.
Sec. 3. (a) Except as provided in subsection (b), the city
admissions tax equals twelve percent (12%) of the price for
admission to any event described in section 2 of this chapter. If the
fiscal body of the city adopts an ordinance under this subsection:
(1) the fiscal body shall immediately send a certified copy of
the ordinance to the commissioner of the department of state
revenue; and
(2) the tax applies to transactions after the last day of the
month in which the ordinance is adopted, if the fiscal body
adopts the ordinance on or before the fifteenth day of a
month. If the fiscal body adopts the ordinance after the
fifteenth day of a month, the tax applies to transactions after
the last day of the month following the month in which the
ordinance is adopted.
(b) The amount collected from the city admissions tax imposed
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

88
shall be distributed to the northwest Indiana stadium board or its
designee. So long as there are any current or future obligations
owed by the northwest Indiana stadium board to the northwest
Indiana stadium authority created by IC 5-1-17.1 or any state
agency pursuant to a lease or other agreement entered into
between the northwest Indiana stadium board and the northwest
Indiana stadium authority or any state agency under IC 5-1-17.1,
the northwest Indiana stadium board or its designee shall deposit
the revenues received from the admissions tax imposed under
subsection (a) in a special fund, which may be used only for the
payment of the obligations described in this subsection.
Sec. 4. (a) Each person who pays a price for admission to any
event described in section 2(a) of this chapter is liable for the tax
imposed under this chapter.
(b) The person who collects the price for admission shall also
collect the city admissions tax imposed with respect to the price for
admission. The person shall collect the tax at the same time the
price for admission is paid, regardless of whether the price paid is
for a single admission, for season tickets, or for any other
admission arrangement, not including those described in section
2(b) of this chapter. In addition, the person shall collect the tax as
an agent of the state and the city in which the facility described in
section 2 of this chapter is located.
Sec. 5. A person who collects any city admission tax under
section 4 of this chapter shall remit the tax collections to the
department of state revenue. The person shall remit those revenues
collected during a particular month before the fifteenth day of the
following month. At the time the tax revenues are remitted, the
person shall file a city admissions tax return on the form
prescribed by the department of state revenue.
Sec. 6. (a) If there are not obligations of the board described in
section 3(b) of this chapter then outstanding and there are no
bonds, leases, or other obligations then outstanding for which a
pledge has been made under section 3(b) of this chapter, the fiscal
body may adopt an ordinance that repeals the ordinance adopted
under section 2 of this chapter.
(b) An ordinance adopted under subsection (a) takes effect on
January 1 immediately following the date of its adoption. If the
fiscal body adopts such an ordinance, the clerk shall immediately
send a certified copy of the ordinance to the commissioner of the
department of state revenue.
(c) A tax imposed under this chapter terminates January 1 of
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

89
the year immediately following the year in which the last payment
obligation of the board is made with respect to any bond, lease, or
other obligation described in section 3(b) of this chapter.

ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

be necessary or desirable in the judgment of the authority to

(7) Make and enter into all contracts and agreements necessary or
incidental to the performance of its duties and the execution of its
powers under this chapter, IC 8-9.5-8, or IC 8-15.5. When the cost
under any such contract or agreement, other than:
(A) a contract for compensation for personal services;
(B) a contract with the department under IC 8-9.5-8-7;
(C) a lease with the department under IC 8-9.5-8-8; or
(D) a contract, a lease, or another agreement under IC 8-15.5;
involves an expenditure of more than ten thousand dollars
($10,000), the authority shall make a written contract with the
lowest and best bidder after advertisement for not less than two
(2) consecutive weeks in a newspaper of general circulation in

authority shall determine. Such notice shall state the general
character of the work and the general character of the materials to
be furnished, the place where plans and specifications therefor
may be examined, and the time and place of receiving bids. Each
bid shall contain the full name of every person or company
interested in it and shall be accompanied by a sufficient bond or
certified check on a solvent bank that if the bid is accepted a
contract will be entered into and the performance of its proposal
secured. The authority may reject any and all bids. A bond with
good and sufficient surety shall be required by the authority of all
contractors in an amount equal to at least fifty percent (50%) of
the contract price, conditioned upon the faithful performance of
the contract. The authority shall require a bid, performance, and
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

91
payment bond from a contractor for a project if the estimated cost
of the project is more than two hundred thousand dollars
($200,000). The authority may require a bid, performance, or
payment bond from a contractor for a project if the estimated cost
of the project is not more than two hundred thousand dollars
($200,000).
(8) Employ consulting engineers, superintendents, managers, and
such other engineers, construction and accounting experts, bond
counsel, other attorneys with the approval of the attorney general,
and other employees and agents as may be necessary in its
judgment to carry out the provisions of this chapter, and to fix
their compensation. However, all such expenses shall be payable
solely from the proceeds of toll road revenue bonds issued under
the provisions of this chapter or from revenues.
(9) Receive and accept from any federal agency, subject to
IC 8-23-3, grants for or in aid of the construction of any toll road
project, and receive and accept aid or contributions from any
source of either money, property, labor, or other things of value,
to be held, used, and applied only for the purposes for which such
grants and contributions may be made, and repay any grant to the
authority or to the department from a federal agency if such
repayment is necessary to free the authority from restrictions
which the authority determines to be in the public interest to
remove.
(10) Establish fees, charges, terms, or conditions for any
expenditures, loans, or other form of financial participation in
projects authorized as public improvements on arterial streets and
roads under section 1 of this chapter.
(11) Accept gifts, devises, bequests, grants, loans, appropriations,
revenue sharing, other financing and assistance, and any other aid
from any source and agree to and comply with conditions attached
to the aid.
(12) Accept transfer of a state highway to the authority under
IC 8-23-7-23 and pay the cost of conversion of the state highway
to a toll road project.
(13) Enter into contracts or leases with the department under
IC 8-9.5-8-7 or IC 8-9.5-8-8 and in connection with the contracts
or leases agree with the department for coordination of the
operation and the repair and maintenance of toll road projects and
tollways which are contiguous parts of the same public road,
including joint toll collection facilities and equitable division of
tolls.
ES 27—LS 6062/DI 13

92
(14) Enter into public-private agreements under IC 8-15.5 and do
all acts and things necessary or proper to carry out the purposes
set forth in IC 8-15.5.
(15) Adopt rules under IC 4-22-2 in the manner provided in
IC 5-1.2-4-1(a)(2) to make changes to rules related to a toll road
project to accommodate the provisions of a public-private
agreement under IC 8-15.5. to which the authority is a party
under IC 8-15.5 and that was originally entered into before
January 1, 2010.
(16) Do all acts and things necessary or proper to carry out this
chapter.
